                  <form>       
                     <itype>6</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">التَّعَافِى</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> signifies [<hi rend="ital">The forgiving,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pardoning, one another,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">the turning away from punishing one another:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">تَعَافَوُا الحُدُودَ فِيمَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَيْنَكُمْ</foreign>, originally <foreign lang="ar">تَعَافَوْا عَنِ الحُدُودِ</foreign>, [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Relinquish ye the prescribed punishments in respect of what occurs between you,</hi>] means <hi rend="ital">let every one of you turn away from</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">relinquish</hi>] <hi rend="ital">punishing his fellow;</hi> the phrase being elliptical, or the verb being made to imply the meaning of <foreign lang="ar">التَّرْك</foreign>, and therefore being made trans. in the same manner as <foreign lang="ar">الترك</foreign>: [hence,] <foreign lang="ar">لَوْ تَعَافَيْتُهَا</foreign> is used by El- Hareeree as meaning <hi rend="ital">If I relinquished them:</hi> (Har p. 60:) [and hence it is said that <foreign lang="ar">التَّعَافِى</foreign> signifies <foreign lang="ar">التَّجَاوُزُ</foreign> [app. when each is followed by <foreign lang="ar">عَنْ</foreign>, and thus meaning <hi rend="ital">The passing by,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">over,</hi> another, or one another, <hi rend="ital">without punishing</hi>]. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  And it signifies also <hi rend="ital">The finding, experiencing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">obtaining, health,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">soundness.</hi> (KL.)    </entryFree>26:T4df3,<entryFree id="n29771" key="عَفَا" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَفَا</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَعْفُو</foreign>, (S, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَفَآءٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">عُفُوٌّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَفْوٌ</foreign>, (Msb, K,) <hi rend="ital">It was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, effaced, erased, rased,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">obliterated;</hi> (S, Msb, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29771-1" target="تعفّى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (K:) and <hi rend="ital">it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he, perished, came to nought</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to an end,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">died.</hi> (S, TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">عَفَا الأَثَرُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The trace, vestige,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">footprint, was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, effaced,</hi> &amp;c. (TA.) And [hence,] <foreign lang="ar">عَفَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَثَرُهُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَفَآءٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He perished,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">died.</hi> (K.) And <foreign lang="ar">عَفَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَنْزِلُ</foreign>, aor. as above. (S, Msb,) and so the inf. ns. as in the first sentence, (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">the place of alighting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode, was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became effaced,</hi> &amp;c., (S, Msb:) and <foreign lang="ar">عَفَت الدَّارُ</foreign>. aor. <foreign lang="ar">تعْفُو</foreign>, inf. a <foreign lang="ar">عَفَآءٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عُفُوٌّ</foreign> [and <foreign lang="ar">عَفْوٌ</foreign>]: (TA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29771-2" target="تَعَفَّت" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (S, TA.) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29771-3" target="عَفَّت" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> also; (TA;) <hi rend="ital">The house,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dwelling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode, was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, effaced,</hi> &amp;c. (S, TA) A'Obeyd cites, as an ex. of <foreign lang="ar">العَفَآءُ</foreign> signifying <hi rend="ital">the being,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">becoming, effaced,</hi> &amp;c., and <hi rend="ital">the perishing,</hi> &amp;c., the saying of Zuheyr, (S, TA.) mentioning a dwelling, or an abode, (TA.) <quote>

                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Its occupants departed from it, and separated themselves,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">removed far away; may the state of that which is effaced,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">be</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rest, upon the traces of what has gone away;</hi> or the meaning may be, <hi rend="ital">dust is upon the traces</hi> &amp;c., (see <foreign lang="ar">عَفَآءٌ</foreign> as a subst., below;) but it is not thus accord to A 'Obeyd; for] he says, This is like their saying <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ الدَّبَارُ</foreign> as an imprecation against one expressing a prayer that he may go away and <hi rend="ital">not return.</hi> (S, TA.) MF says that <foreign lang="ar">عَفَا</foreign> is one of those verbs that have contr. significations, for at signifies <hi rend="ital">It was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, unapparent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">imperceptible</hi> and also <hi rend="ital">It was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, apparent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">perceptible:</hi> and it has two other contr. significations, which will be mentioned in what follows (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">عَفْوٌ</foreign> signifies also The act of <hi rend="ital">effacing, erasing, rasing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">obliterating.</hi> (K, TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">عَفَتِ الرِّيحُ الأَثَرَ</foreign>, (TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">المَنْزِلَ</foreign>, (S, Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">الدَّارَ</foreign>, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">the wind effaced,</hi> &amp;c, (S, Msb, TA,) <hi rend="ital">the trace, vestige,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">footprint,</hi> (TA,) or <hi rend="ital">the place of alighting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode,</hi> (S, Msb,) and <hi rend="ital">the house,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dwelling,</hi> or <pb n="2093"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">abode:</hi> (TA:) and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29771-4" target="عَفَّتِ" n="4" type="8" subtype="FSOTF" lang="ar"/>الرِّيحُ الدَّارَ</foreign>, (S, TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَعْفِيَةٌ</foreign>, (TA,) in which the verb is with teshdeed to denote intensiveness [of the signification, i. e. <hi rend="ital">the wind effaced,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">mightily,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">utterly, the house,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dwelling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode</hi>]: (S, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29771-5" target="عَفَّى" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>عَلَى أَثَرِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">It,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he, effaced its,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">his, trace, vestige,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">footprint.</hi> (MA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Hence, as some say, <foreign lang="ar">عَفَا ٱللّٰهُ عَنْكَ</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">May God efface</hi> [<hi rend="ital">from thee</hi> thy sin, &amp;c.; meaning <hi rend="ital">may God absolve thee</hi>]; (TA;) or <hi rend="ital">may God efface thy sins:</hi> (Msb:) [and <foreign lang="ar">عُفِىَ عَنْهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">May he be absolved,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">forgiven,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pardoned:</hi>] and hence the saying in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">سَلُوا ٱللّٰهَ العَفْوَ</foreign> i. e.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29771-6" target="المُعَافَاةَ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, and

rend="ital">the relinquishing the punishment of the deserving</hi> [<hi rend="ital">thereof</hi>]: and one says, <foreign lang="ar">عَفَا عَنْهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَفَا لَهُ                         <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا تَنْطِقِى فِى سَوْرَتِى حِينَ أَغْضَبُ</foreign>

(S.) <foreign lang="ar">قُلِ العَفْوَ</foreign>, in the Kur [ii. 217], means <hi rend="ital">Say thou,</hi> Expend ye <hi rend="ital">what is redundant and abundant.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">خُدِ العَفْوَ</foreign>, in the same [vii. 198]. means [<hi rend="ital">Take thou,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">accept thou,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">what is redundant:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">accept thou what is easily obtained from the dispositions of men;</hi> and oppose them not, for in that case they would oppose thee, and thence would be engendered hatred and enmity. [<hi rend="ital">I gave him, of the property, that for which he did not ask;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">spontaneously;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">without being asked.</hi> (S.)                   <hi rend="ital">He attained the thing easily.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَتَانِى ذٰلِكَ</foreign>
